        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>



<br>





In class FileSystemAccessManagerImpl, there is a raw pointer:



<span class="line"><!---->In class FileSystemAccessManagerImpl, there is a raw pointer:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





"""



<span class="line"><!---->"""<!----></span>



<br>





FileSystemAccessPermissionContext* permission_context_;



<span class="line"><!---->FileSystemAccessPermissionContext* permission_context_;<!----></span>



<br>





"""



<span class="line"><!---->"""<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





`permission_context_` is owned by StoragePartitionImpl, on the other hand, FileSystemAccessManagerImpl is owned by StoragePartitionImpl too from annotation(in face it is NOT):



<span class="line"><!---->`permission_context_` is owned by StoragePartitionImpl, on the other hand, FileSystemAccessManagerImpl is owned by StoragePartitionImpl too from annotation(in face it is NOT):<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





"""



<span class="line"><!---->"""<!----></span>



<br>





// This is the browser side implementation of the



<span class="line"><!---->// This is the browser side implementation of the<!----></span>



<br>





// FileSystemAccessManager mojom interface. This is the main entry point for



<span class="line"><!---->// FileSystemAccessManager mojom interface. This is the main entry point for<!----></span>



<br>





// the File System Access API in the browser process.Instances of this class are



<span class="line"><!---->// the File System Access API in the browser process.Instances of this class are<!----></span>



<br>





// owned by StoragePartitionImpl.



<span class="line"><!---->// owned by StoragePartitionImpl.<!----></span>



<br>





"""



<span class="line"><!---->"""<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So in normal situation, the raw pointer `permission_context_` in FileSystemAccessManagerImpl is safe. But FileSystemAccessManagerImpl is a RefCountedThreadSafe object so in special situation, we can add ref to it and outlives of StoragePartitionImpl, and the raw pointer `permission_context_` becomes dangling pointer.



<span class="line"><!---->So in normal situation, the raw pointer `permission_context_` in FileSystemAccessManagerImpl is safe. But FileSystemAccessManagerImpl is a RefCountedThreadSafe object so in special situation, we can add ref to it and outlives of StoragePartitionImpl, and the raw pointer `permission_context_` becomes dangling pointer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In function `FileSystemAccessManagerImpl::DidVerifySensitiveDirectoryAccess`, there are some `base::BindOnce` call with argument `this`, this will add ref of FileSystemAccessManagerImpl. 



<span class="line"><!---->In function `FileSystemAccessManagerImpl::DidVerifySensitiveDirectoryAccess`, there are some `base::BindOnce` call with argument `this`, this will add ref of FileSystemAccessManagerImpl. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





"""



<span class="line"><!---->"""<!----></span>



<br>





 operation_runner().PostTaskWithThisObject(



<span class="line"><!----> operation_runner().PostTaskWithThisObject(<!----></span>



<br>





        FROM_HERE,



<span class="line"><!---->        FROM_HERE,<!----></span>



<br>





        base::BindOnce(



<span class="line"><!---->        base::BindOnce(<!----></span>



<br>





            &CreateAndTruncateFile, fs_url,



<span class="line"><!---->            &amp;CreateAndTruncateFile, fs_url,<!----></span>



<br>





            base::BindOnce(



<span class="line"><!---->            base::BindOnce(<!----></span>



<br>





                &FileSystemAccessManagerImpl::DidCreateAndTruncateSaveFile,



<span class="line"><!---->                &amp;FileSystemAccessManagerImpl::DidCreateAndTruncateSaveFile,<!----></span>



<br>





                this, binding_context, entries.front(), fs_url,



<span class="line"><!---->                this, binding_context, entries.front(), fs_url,<!----></span>



<br>





                std::move(callback)),



<span class="line"><!---->                std::move(callback)),<!----></span>



<br>





            base::SequencedTaskRunnerHandle::Get()));



<span class="line"><!---->            base::SequencedTaskRunnerHandle::Get()));<!----></span>



<br>





"""



<span class="line"><!---->"""<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So consider below situation, uaf will happen:



<span class="line"><!---->So consider below situation, uaf will happen:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. call above BindOnce function, ref count is 2, and then post task DidCreateAndTruncateSaveFile.



<span class="line"><!---->1. call above BindOnce function, ref count is 2, and then post task DidCreateAndTruncateSaveFile.<!----></span>



<br>





2. call ~StoragePartitionImpl, frees FileSystemAccessPermissionContext, and `permission_context_` becomes dangling pointer, FileSystemAccessManagerImpl's ref count is 1 so it still lives.



<span class="line"><!---->2. call ~StoragePartitionImpl, frees FileSystemAccessPermissionContext, and `permission_context_` becomes dangling pointer, FileSystemAccessManagerImpl's ref count is 1 so it still lives.<!----></span>



<br>





3. call `DidCreateAndTruncateSaveFile` => `GetSharedHandleStateForPath` => `permission_context_->GetReadPermissionGrant` and uaf happens.



<span class="line"><!---->3. call `DidCreateAndTruncateSaveFile` =&gt; `GetSharedHandleStateForPath` =&gt; `permission_context_-&gt;GetReadPermissionGrant` and uaf happens.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





how to reproduce:



<span class="line"><!---->how to reproduce:<!----></span>



<br>





$python ./copy_mojo_js_bindings.py /path/to/chrome/.../out/Debug/gen



<span class="line"><!---->$python ./copy_mojo_js_bindings.py /path/to/chrome/.../out/Debug/gen<!----></span>



<br>





$out/Debug/chrome --enable-blink-features=MojoJS  127.0.0.1:8000/1.html



<span class="line"><!---->$out/Debug/chrome --enable-blink-features=MojoJS  127.0.0.1:8000/1.html<!----></span>



<br>





$click trigger, wait about 4-8 seconds(it need to race here and depend on hardware, so may be it is not stable to reproduce, if you can't, change the time here), and click confirm save file.



<span class="line"><!---->$click trigger, wait about 4-8 seconds(it need to race here and depend on hardware, so may be it is not stable to reproduce, if you can't, change the time here), and click confirm save file.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The fix:



<span class="line"><!---->The fix:<!----></span>



<br>





I think the FileSystemAccessManagerImpl need to create a `Shutdown` function like FileSystemContext and ~StoragePartitionImpl will call it. In `Shutdown` function, it will clear the raw pointer `permission_context_`. There are many places like `if (permission_context_)` in FileSystemAccessManagerImpl's methods, so I think you may be forget to create a `Shuntdown` function for FileSystemAccessManagerImpl.



<span class="line"><!---->I think the FileSystemAccessManagerImpl need to create a `Shutdown` function like FileSystemContext and ~StoragePartitionImpl will call it. In `Shutdown` function, it will clear the raw pointer `permission_context_`. There are many places like `if (permission_context_)` in FileSystemAccessManagerImpl's methods, so I think you may be forget to create a `Shuntdown` function for FileSystemAccessManagerImpl.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





*Please note that this bug may be can trigger with normal render process(not compromised) as the mojo interfaces can be called from web API. I use MojoJS just a convenience and for race more stable. It is not necessary.



<span class="line"><!---->*Please note that this bug may be can trigger with normal render process(not compromised) as the mojo interfaces can be called from web API. I use MojoJS just a convenience and for race more stable. It is not necessary.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





As it need to race to trigger the bug, so may be it is not stable to reproduce, please try more times. But the bug is clear in code.



<span class="line"><!---->As it need to race to trigger the bug, so may be it is not stable to reproduce, please try more times. But the bug is clear in code.<!----></span>



<br>

<span class="line"><!---->Whilst I can't reproduce this, the description of the root cause behind the UaF is very clear and meets the bar for us to pass this on beyond the security team.<!----></span>

Severity:



<span class="line"><!---->Severity:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Browser process UaF, triggerable via Mojo from renderer process => high severity.



<span class="line"><!---->Browser process UaF, triggerable via Mojo from renderer process =&gt; high severity.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The stack traces provided suggest that this happens on profile destruction only. It shouldn't normally be possible for a website to cause this; the site has to induce the user to close a window (e.g. an Incognito window). Therefore we usually mitigate profile destruction bugs down by a level => rating this medium.



<span class="line"><!---->The stack traces provided suggest that this happens on profile destruction only. It shouldn't normally be possible for a website to cause this; the site has to induce the user to close a window (e.g. an Incognito window). Therefore we usually mitigate profile destruction bugs down by a level =&gt; rating this medium.<!----></span>

 - OK, I learned today that websites can self-close if they are opened from the command-line. window.close() did indeed work when the site was opened that way. <span class="line"><!---->Before a merge request will be considered, the following information is required to be added to this bug:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1. Does your merge fit within the Merge Decision Guidelines?



<span class="line"><!---->1. Does your merge fit within the Merge Decision Guidelines?<!----></span>

- Chrome: 



<span class="line"><!---->- Chrome: <!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->2. Links to the CLs you are requesting to merge.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->3. Has the change landed and been verified on ToT?<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->4. Does this change need to be merged into other active release branches (M-1, M+1)?<!----></span>



<br>





5. Why are these changes required in this milestone after branch?



<span class="line"><!---->5. Why are these changes required in this milestone after branch?<!----></span>



<br>





6. Is this a new feature?



<span class="line"><!---->6. Is this a new feature?<!----></span>



<br>





7. If it is a new feature, is it behind a flag using finch?



<span class="line"><!---->7. If it is a new feature, is it behind a flag using finch?<!----></span>

<br>





Chrome OS Only:



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome OS Only:<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }

          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
